Qada of Missed Prayers for an Unconscious Person
Ruling with proof from athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for missed prayers due to unconsciousness and apply the one-day-one-night threshold, citing the athar from Ibn Umar and the principle of raf' al-haraj.

Core Idea
Unconsciousness up to a day and night requires qada; beyond that, it is waived to remove hardship.

In the Hanafi school, the obligation to make up missed prayers is not absolute for every situation of unconsciousness. This lesson examines the precise threshold of one day and one night, established by the practice of the Companion Abdullah ibn Umar and reinforced by the legal maxim of removing hardship. Understanding this ruling prevents both neglect of necessary qada and undue burden beyond what the Shari'ah requires.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up (qada) missed obligatory prayers. The ruling is wajib if unconsciousness lasted ≤ 1 day and night; otherwise no qada.
The duration is measured from loss to recovery of consciousness.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The primary evidence is the action of Abdullah ibn Umar, who did not make up prayers after being unconscious for a day and night or for a month, as recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
This is a qawl sahabi, accepted as proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the rationale
Requiring qada for long unconsciousness would cause extreme hardship (haraj), which is lifted by Islamic law. This parallels the exemption for menstruating women.
The principle 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' supports removal of obligation when impossible.
4
Distinguish from sleep
Sleep is temporary; the obligation remains. Unconsciousness beyond a day and night removes the obligation entirely, unlike sleep where qada is always required.
The hadith 'The Pen is lifted from three...' includes the sleeping person until they wake, but that applies to sin, not qada of missed acts.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a specific duration of unconsciousness, apply the threshold: if ≤ day and night → qada wajib; if more → no qada.
The exact start and end times must be determined carefully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل) ۲۱۵ كتاب الصلوة عليه خمس صلوات فما دونها قضاها اذا صح وان فاتته بالاغماء اكثر من ذلك لم يقض نیند کے درجہ میں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی نماز قضا کرے گا۔ اور ایک دن ایک رات سے زیادہ بیہوشی رہی تو اس سے خطاب اٹھا ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے اب اس کی نماز قضا نہیں کرے گا (۲) اس طرح قضا کروائیں تو حرج لازم ہوگا تو جس طرح حائضہ سے نماز معاف ہے اسی طرح اس سے بھی نماز معاف ہوگی ۔ (۳) آثار میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر عن نافع قال اغمى على ابن عمر يوما وليلة فلم يقض مـا فـاتـه ... وفي حديث آخر ... ان ابن عمر اغمی علیه شهرا فلم يقض ما فاته وصلى يومه الذي افاق فيه (الف) (مصنف عبد ارزاق، باب صلوۃ المریض علی الدابة وصلوۃ اسمی علیہ ج ثانی ص ۴۷۹ نمبر ۴۱۵۳/۴۱۵۲) ان دونوں آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک دن ایک رات کی نماز سے قضا ہوئی ہو تو قضا کرے گا اور زیادہ ہوئی ہو تو قضا نہیں کرے گا۔ معاف ہے ورنہ حرج لازم ہو گا ۔ حاشیہ : (الف) عبداللہ ابن عمر پر ایک دن ایک رات بیہوشی طاری ہوئی تو جو نمازیں فوت ہوئی اس کی قضا نہیں کی۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ ابن عمر پر ایک ماہ تک بیہوشی طاری ہوئی تو جو نماز میں فوت ہوئیں ان کی قضا نہیں کی۔ اور اس دن کی نماز پڑھی جس دن افاقہ ہوا۔
The commentary on al-Thamiri, part one, p. 215, Book of Prayer. He has five prayers and what is less than that, he makes them up when he recovers, and if he missed more than that due to unconsciousness, he does not make them up. It is like the state of sleep. Therefore, he will make up his prayer. And if unconsciousness lasted more than one day and one night, then the address (obligation) is lifted from him. Therefore, he will not make up his prayer now. (2) If we require him to make up, then hardship (haraj) would necessarily result, so just as a menstruating woman is excused from prayer, likewise he is excused. (3) There are athar: from Abdullah ibn Umar from Nafi: Ibn Umar was unconscious for a day and a night, so he did not make up what he missed... And in another hadith: Ibn Umar was unconscious for a month, so he did not make up what he missed, and he prayed on the day he regained consciousness. (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on prayer of the sick on an animal and prayer of ...? vol. 2, p. 479, no. 4153/4152). From these two athar it is understood that if missed prayers are up to a day and night, he will make them up, and if more, he will not make them up. They are excused, otherwise hardship would be necessary. Footnote: (a) Abdullah ibn Umar became unconscious for a day and a night, so the prayers that were missed were not made up by him. In another hadith: Ibn Umar became unconscious for a month, so the prayers that were missed were not made up, and he prayed on the day he recovered.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the issue of qada (making up) of missed prayers for a person who becomes unconscious. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: if the unconsciousness lasts for a period of a day and a night or less, then upon recovery, the person must make up the missed prayers. This is because the obligation (khitab) remains, similar to one who sleeps. If unconsciousness exceeds a day and a night, the obligation is lifted, and no qada is required. The rationale is that requiring qada would cause excessive hardship (haraj), analogous to the exemption given to a menstruating woman. The proof is provided through two athar (reports) from Ibn Umar: in one, he was unconscious for a day and a night and did not make up the missed prayers; in another, he was unconscious for a month and only prayed on the day he recovered, not making up the prior missed prayers. The commentator notes that the threshold is specifically one day and one night: more than that is excused.

Key Terms
اغماء (ighmā'): Unconsciousness, a state where a person is unaware and unable to perform obligations.
قضا (qaḍā): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship after its time has passed.
حرج (ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty, a basis for lifting obligations in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a person is unconscious for more than one full day and night, what is the ruling on the missed prayers?
A) They must make up all missed prayers after recovery.
B) They do not need to make up any missed prayers.
C) They only need to make up the prayers of the first day.
D) They must make up the prayers if they intended to pray before unconsciousness.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets a limit of one day and one night for qada of prayers missed due to unconsciousness, based on the practice of Ibn Umar and the principle of avoiding hardship.

Sujud al-Tilawah: Obligation, Number, and the Maliki Dispute
Definition and proofs of sajdat al-tilawah, number of verses, and obligation for reciter and listener

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujud al-tilawah, identify the fourteen verses, and explain why the second prostration in Surah al-Hajj is not wajib, using the Hanafi proofs and rebuttal to the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib for reciter and listener; Hanafis hold 14 prostrations, with the second in al-Hajj for teaching only.

This passage from the commentary on al-Sameri establishes the ruling on the prostration of recitation. You will learn the number of obligatory prostrations according to the Hanafi school, the proof for their obligation, and a key inter-madhhab dispute with the Maliki school regarding Surah al-Hajj. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting evidence (ta'arud al-adillah) and appreciate the Hanafi methodology of relying on the practice of the Companions and the Tabi'un.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (sajdat al-tilawah) and its legal status (wajib) according to the Hanafi school.
The text opens by stating there are 14 prostrations, implying obligation.
2
Locate the proof for obligation
Find the primary hadith evidence cited (Ibn Abbas on the Prophet prostrating in al-Najm) and analyze how it proves obligation.
The fact that the Prophet prostrated and others followed indicates a prescriptive action.
3
List the fourteen verses
Identify the specific surahs and verses enumerated in the text. Note that the first in al-Hajj is included, but not the second.
Memorizing this list is foundational for practice.
4
Analyze the dispute in Surah al-Hajj
Compare the Hanafi position (one prostration, second for teaching) with the Maliki position (two prostrations, both wajib). Identify each school's evidence.
The Hanafi proof relies on athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, al-Hasan, and Ibn Abbas. The Maliki proof relies on the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn Amir.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis rebut the Maliki hadith: they interpret it as indicating permissibility or teaching, not obligation, and give priority to the practice of the Companions.
The thamarah al-khilaf: missing the second prostration is not sinful for Hanafis, but is for Malikis.

،مشرکین ، جنات اور انسان نے بھی سجدہ کیا (ب) سعید بن مسیب اور حسن نے فرمایا کہ سورۂ حج میں ایک سجدہ ہے۔ان میں سے پہلا سجدہ (ج) ابن عباس نے فرمایا سورہ حج میں پہلا سجدہ تاکیدی ہے اور دوسرا سجدہ تعلیم کے لئے ہے۔ اور اس میں سجدہ نہیں کیا کرتے تھے (د) میں نے حضور سے کہا کہ سورہ حج میں دو سجدے ہیں ؟ تو آپ نے فرمایا ہاں! اور جس نے دو سجدے نہیں کئے تو گویا کہ ان کو پڑھا ہی نہیں۔
Chapter on the Prostration of Recitation. [319] (1) In the Quran there are fourteen prostrations: at the end of al-A'raf, in al-Ra'd, in al-Nahl, in Bani Isra'il, in Maryam, and the first in al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Inshiqaq, and al-Alaq. (320)(2) Necessary note: In the Noble Quran there are fourteen verses, upon reciting which prostration becomes obligatory. They are called sajdat al-tilawah. The proof that sajdat al-tilawah is obligatory is from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet prostrated in Surah al-Najm, and with him prostrated the Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans.' (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on sajdat al-Najm, p. 146, no. 071; and Sahih Muslim, chapter on sujud al-tilawah? p. 215, no. 576). This hadith proves that upon reciting a verse of prostration, one should prostrate. And also those who listen should prostrate. [319] (1) There are prostrations on fourteen verses in the Quran: (1) at the end of Surah al-A'raf, (2) al-Ra'd, (3) al-Nahl, (4) Bani Isra'il, (5) Maryam, (6) the first in Surah al-Hajj, (7) al-Furqan, (8) al-Naml, (9) al-Tanzil, (10) Sad, (11) Ha Mim al-Sajdah, (12) al-Najm, (13) al-Inshiqaq, (14) al-Alaq. These are fourteen verses, upon reciting which prostration is obligatory for the reciter. According to the Hanafis, in Surah al-Hajj, the first prostration triggers obligation. The proof is this athar: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and al-Hasan: they said that in al-Hajj there is one prostration, the first of them. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter ...? no. 3300). (2) from Ibn Abbas: he said that in Surah al-Hajj, the first is a determined (azima) prostration and the last is for teaching, and he did not prostrate in it. (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on how many prostrations in the Quran, no. 5892). From these two athar it is understood that in Surah al-Hajj, the first verse has a prostration, and the second verse is for teaching. Rather, according to Imam Malik, there are prostrations in both places. His proof is the hadith: 'Uqbah ibn Amir narrated: I said to the Messenger of Allah, 'In Surah al-Hajj there are two prostrations?' He said, 'Yes, and whoever does not prostrate them, then he has not recited them.' (d) (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on how many prostrations in the Quran, no. 1402; and in Tirmidhi, chapter on prostration in al-Hajj, no. 578). This hadith proves that there are two prostrations in Surah al-Hajj. On this basis, the total prostrations become fifteen. That is the statement of Imam Malik. [320] (2) The prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter and upon the listener, whether he intended to listen to the Quran or not. Upon reciting these verses, both the reciter and the listener are obligated to prostrate, whether they intended to listen or not. The proof for obligation is this athar: from Ibn Abbas: he said, 'Sad is not among the determined (azaim) prostrations, and I saw the Prophet prostrating in it.' Footnote: (a) He prostrated in Surah al-Najm, and with him prostrated Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans. (b) Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and al-Hasan said: in Surah al-Hajj there is one prostration, the first of them. (c) Ibn Abbas said: in Surah al-Hajj, the first is a confirmed prostration, and the last is for teaching, and he used not to prostrate in it. (d) I said to the Prophet: 'In Surah al-Hajj there are two prostrations?' He said, 'Yes, and whoever does not prostrate both, then it is as if he has not recited them.'
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and a ruling. It begins by introducing the chapter on sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The text first states the Hanafi position: there are fourteen prostrations in the Quran, listing them by surah. It then provides the proof for the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah from the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prostrated upon reciting Surah al-Najm, and others joined him. The obligation applies to both the reciter and the listener. The text then details the Hanafi view on the dispute regarding the number of prostrations in Surah al-Hajj: the Hanafis hold that only the first verse is a prostration of obligation (azima), while the second is for teaching. This is supported by athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and al-Hasan, and from Ibn Abbas. On the other hand, Imam Malik holds that there are two prostrations in Surah al-Hajj, citing a hadith from 'Uqbah ibn Amir where the Prophet affirmed two prostrations. The Hanafis counter that the second prostration is not obligatory. Finally, the passage reaffirms that sajdah is wajib upon the reciter and listener regardless of intent, with proof from another hadith regarding Surah Sad.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that is prescribed.
عزيمة (ʿazīmah): A determined or confirmed obligation, as opposed to a mere teaching or recommendation.
تعليم (taʿlīm): Teaching or instructional; used to describe the second prostration in Surah al-Hajj according to the Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many sajdat al-tilawah are there in the Quran, and what is the status of the second prostration in Surah al-Hajj?
A) 15 prostrations; the second in al-Hajj is wajib.
B) 14 prostrations; the second in al-Hajj is for teaching and not wajib.
C) 14 prostrations; both in al-Hajj are wajib.
D) 15 prostrations; only the first in al-Hajj is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes 14 wajib prostrations; the second in al-Hajj is not obligatory but for teaching.

Number of Sajda Verses: The Hanafi-Maliki Dispute on Surah al-Hajj
States the fourteen sajda verses and the dispute with Imam Malik over surah al-Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the fourteen sajda verses and explain the Maliki objection regarding Surah al-Hajj, identifying the key proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Hanafis count 14 sajda verses; Malikis count 15 due to two sajdas in Surah al-Hajj.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known inter-madhhab dispute concerning the number of obligatory prostrations of recitation (sujud al-tilawah) in the Quran. The Hanafi school affirms fourteen sajda verses, while the Maliki school holds that Surah al-Hajj contains two sajdas, bringing the total to fifteen. Through the source passage, we will explore the evidence from athar and hadith that underpin each position and understand the practical difference in worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school counts 14 sajda verses; Surah al-Hajj has only one sajda (the first verse).
The list of 14 verses is provided in the passage.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that Surah al-Hajj has two sajdas, making the total 15.
The Maliki view is based on a hadith from Uqba ibn Amir.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Maliki proof is a hadith where the Prophet (saw) confirmed two sajdas in al-Hajj.
Refer to Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis cite athar that indicate only the first sajda is binding (azima); the second is for teaching (ta'lim).
Ibn Abbas did not prostrate at the second verse.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis prostrate at 14 places; Malikis at 15.
This affects recitation in and out of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
باب سجود التلاوة
[۳۱۹ (۱) فى القرآن اربعة عشر سجدة في آخر الاعراف وفى الرعد وفي النحل وفي بنی اسرائیل و مريم والاولى فى الحج والفرقان والنمل والانشقاق والعلق (۳۲۰)(۲)
باب سجود التلاوة کے ضروری نوٹ قرآن کریم میں چودہ آیتیں ہیں جن کے پڑھنے سے سجدہ کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ ان کو سجدہ تلاوت کہتے ہیں۔ سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہونے کی یہ دلیل ہے عن ابن عباس ان النبى الله مسجد بالنجم وسجد معه المسلمون والمشركون والجن والانس (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب سجدة النجم ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۰۷۱ ار مسلم شریف ، باب مسجود التلاو ق ص ۲۱۵ نمبر ۵۷۶) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے سجدہ کرنا چاہئے ۔ اور جو لوگ سے ان کو بھی سجدہ کرنا چاہئے۔
[۳۱۹] (۱) قرآن کریم میں چودہ آیتوں پر سجدے ہیں (۱) سورۃ اعراف کے اخیر میں (۲) الرعد (۳) انحل (۴) بنی اسرائیل (۵) مریم (۶) سورہ حج میں پہلا سجدہ (۷) الفرقان (۸) النمل (۹) الم تنزیل (۱۰) ص (۱۱) حم السجدة (۱۲) النجم (۱۳) الانشاق (۱۴) العلق ۔ یہ چودہ آیتیں ہیں جن کے پڑھنے سے پڑھنے والے پر سجدہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ حنفیہ کے نزدیک سورہ حج میں جو پہلا سجدہ ہے اس کے پڑھنے سے سجدہ واجب ہوتا ہے ہے اس کی وجہ یہ اثر ہے عن سعید بن المسیب والحسن قالا في الحج سجدة واحدة الاولى منها (ب)(مصنف بن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۲۱۵ من قال هي واحدة وهی الاولی ، ج اول ص ۳۷۳ نمبر ۳۳۰۰ (۲) عن ابن عباس قال في سورة الحج الاولى عزيمة والآخرة تعليم وكان لا يسجد فيها (ج) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب کم فی القرآن من سجدۃ ص۳۴۲ نمبر ۵۸۹۲) ان دونوں آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورہ حج میں پہلی آیت پر سجدہ ہے دوسری آیت تعلیم کے لئے ہے۔ نا کہ امام مالک کے نزدیک دونوں جگہ سجدے ہیں ان کی دلیل یہ حديث ہے ان عقبة بن عامر حدثه قال قلت لرسول الله في سورة الحج سجدتان قال نعم ومن لم يسجد هما فلا يقرأهما (د) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب کم سجدة في القرآن ص ۲۰۶ نمبر ۱۴۰۲، باب تفریح ابواب السجو در ترندی شریف، باب فی السجدۃ فی الحج ص ۱۲۸ نمبر ۵۷۸) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ سورہ حج میں دو سجدے ہیں۔ اس اعتبار سے کل سجدے پندرہ ہو جائیں گے۔ یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے۔
Book of Prayer. Chapter: Prostration of Recitation. [319 (1)] In the Quran are fourteen prostrations: at the end of al-A'raf, in al-Ra'd, in al-Nahl, in Bani Isra'il, Maryam, the first in al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Inshiqaq, and al-Alaq. [320 (2)] Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah. Essential Notes: In the noble Quran there are fourteen verses whose recitation makes prostration obligatory. This is called Sujud al-Tilawah. The evidence for the obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah is: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (saw) prostrated in Surah al-Najm, and with him prostrated the Muslims, the polytheists, the jinn, and the humans. (Bukhari, Bab Sajdat al-Najm, p. 146 no. 1071; Muslim, Bab Sujud al-Tilawah, p. 215 no. 576). This hadith proves that upon reciting a sajda verse, prostration should be performed. And those who listen to it should also prostrate. [319] (1) In the noble Quran there are sajdas on fourteen verses: (1) at the end of Surah al-A'raf, (2) al-Ra'd, (3) al-Nahl, (4) Bani Isra'il, (5) Maryam, (6) the first sajda in Surah al-Hajj, (7) al-Furqan, (8) al-Naml, (9) al-M Tanzil, (10) Sad, (11) Ha Meem al-Sajda, (12) al-Najm, (13) al-Inshiqaq, (14) al-Alaq. These are fourteen verses upon whose recitation prostration becomes obligatory on the reciter. According to the Hanafis, the first sajda in Surah al-Hajj makes prostration obligatory. The reason for this is the athar: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and al-Hasan: they said: In al-Hajj there is one sajda, the first of them. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, p. 215, no. 3300). And from Ibn Abbas: he said: In Surah al-Hajj, the first is azima (obligatory) and the latter is ta'lim (teaching), and he would not prostrate in it. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, p. 342 no. 5892). From these two athar it is known that in Surah al-Hajj the first verse has a sajda; the second verse is for teaching. Rather, according to Imam Malik, there are sajdas in both places. His evidence is the hadith: from Uqba ibn Amir: he said: I said to the Messenger of Allah: In Surah al-Hajj there are two sajdas? He said: Yes, and whoever does not prostrate them, then he does not recite them. (Abu Dawood, Bab Kam Sajda fi al-Quran, p. 206 no. 1402; Tirmidhi, Bab fi al-Sajda fi al-Hajj, p. 128 no. 578). This hadith proves that in Surah al-Hajj there are two sajdas. According to this, the total sajdas become fifteen. This is the saying of Imam Malik.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of obligatory prostrations of recitation (sujud al-tilawah) in the Quran. The Hanafi school holds that there are fourteen such verses, as listed. The key point of contention is Surah al-Hajj: Hanafis consider only the first verse (ayat 18) to be a sajda verse, while the second (ayat 77) is not. They support this with athar (reports from the Companions and Successors) that indicate the first is 'azima (binding) and the second is 'ta'lim' (instruction). The Maliki school, on the other hand, counts two sajdas in Surah al-Hajj, relying on a hadith from Uqba ibn Amir that the Prophet (saw) affirmed two sajdas. This would make the total fifteen. The passage presents the Hanafi position first, then the Maliki objection, without explicitly preferring one; however, the context implies the Hanafi view is the relied-upon one in this text.

Key Terms
سجدہ تلاوت (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran (ayat al-sajda).
عزیمۃ (azimah): In the context of surah al-Hajj, the first sajda verse is described as 'azima, meaning obligatory and binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many obligatory sajda verses are in the Quran?
A) 14
B) 15
C) 16
D) 13

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school counts 14 sajda verses; the Maliki school counts 15 due to an additional sajda in Surah al-Hajj, a legitimate difference rooted in different evidence.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Obligation of Sujud on Reciter and Listener
Establishes the obligation of sujud al-tilawah on reciter and listener, with Shafi'i counterview.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sujud al-tilawah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib in the Hanafi school — the reciter and listener are both obligated, regardless of intent.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that sujud al-tilawah is wajib on both the reciter and the listener, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view that it is sunnah. Through evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, the Hanafi school establishes obligation, while the Shafi'i school relies on the action of Umar. Understanding this dispute clarifies the practical difference in religious duty.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib on both the reciter and the listener, whether the listener intended to hear or not.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
The Prophet (saw) prostrated in Surah Sad and the companions crowded to prostrate with him, indicating obligation. Also, athar from Ibn Umar and Sa'id ibn Jubayr state that prostration is upon the one who hears.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas uses mafhum mukhalif to emphasize other sajdas.
3
State the opposing position (Shafi'i)
Imam al-Shafi'i holds sujud al-tilawah to be sunnah, not wajib.
4
Identify the opposing dalil
Umar ibn al-Khattab prostrated one Friday and not the next, saying whoever prostrates does well and whoever does not has no sin.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi school argues that Umar's action was a personal ijtihad or due to a valid excuse, not a rejection of obligation. The practical difference (thamarah) is that for Hanafis, omission is sinful; for Shafi'is, it is not.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school remains wujub.

[۳۲۰] (۲) سجدہ واجب ہے ان جگہوں میں پڑھنے والے پر اور سننے والے پر چاہے قرآن سننے کا ارادہ کیا ہو یا ارادہ نہ کیا ہو۔ ان آیتوں کے پڑھنے سے پڑھنے والے اور سننے والے دونوں پر سجدہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ چاہے سننے کی نیت کی ہو یا نہ کی ہو۔ واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن ابن عباس قال ص ليس من عزائم السجود وقد رأيت النبي الله يسجد فيها حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے سجدہ کیا سورہ نجم میں اور آپ کے ساتھ مسلمان ،مشرکین ، جنات اور انسان نے بھی سجدہ کیا (ب) سعید بن مسیب اور حسن نے فرمایا کہ سورۂ حج میں ایک سجدہ ہے۔ان میں سے پہلا سجدہ (ج) ابن عباس نے فرمایا سورہ حج میں پہلا سجدہ تاکیدی ہے اور دوسرا سجدہ تعلیم کے لئے ہے۔ اور اس میں سجدہ نہیں کیا کرتے تھے (د) میں نے حضور سے کہا کہ سورہ حج میں دو سجدے ہیں ؟ تو آپ نے فرمایا ہاں! اور جس نے دو سجدے نہیں کئے تو گویا کہ ان کو پڑھا ہی نہیں۔
والسجود واجب فى هذه المواضع على التالى والسامع سواء قصد سماع القرآن او لم (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب مسجدۃ ص ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۱۰۶۹ / ابوداؤد شریف باب السجود فی ص ص ۳۰۷ نمبر ۱۴۰۹ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی السجدة في ص ص ۱۲۷ نمبر ۵۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورۃ ص میں سجدہ تاکیدی نہیں ہے۔ اس کا مفہوم مخالف یہ ہوگا کہ دوسری آیتوں کا سجدہ تاکیدی ہے اور اس کا نام وجوب ہے۔ اس لئے سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہے۔ ایک اور حدیث سے اس کا اشارہ ملتا ہے عن ابن عمر قال كان النبى الله يقرأ السجدة ونحن عنده فيسجد ونسجد معه فتزدحم حتى ما يجد احدنا لجبهته موضعا يسجد عليه (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب از دحام الناس اذ اقرا الامام السجدۃ ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۰۷۶ ارباب ما جاء في سجود القرآن مسلم شریف، باب سجود التلاوۃ ص ۲۱۵ نمبر ۵۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سجدہ واجب ہے اور سننے والوں پر بھی واجب ہے۔ اسی لئے تو سننے کے بعد تمام لوگ سجدہ کرتے تھے۔ یہاں تک کہ سجدہ کے لئے جگہ باقی نہیں رہتی تھی۔ اس حدیث سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آیت سجدہ سننے کا ارادہ نہ بھی رکھتا ہو تو بھی سننے سے سجدہ واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس میں بہت سے لوگ وہ بھی ہوں گے جو سننے کا ارادہ نہ رکھتے ہوں گے پھر بھی انہوں نے سجدہ کیا (۲) اس اثر سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے عن ابن عمر قال انما السجدة على من سمعها،سعيد بن جبير قال من سمع الـ السجدة فعليه ان يسجد (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۰۷ ، باب من قال السجدة على من جلس لھا و من سمعھ ، اج اول ، ص ۳۶۷ ، نمبر ۴۲۲۲/۴۲۲۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو بھی آیت سجدہ سنے گا اس پر سجدہ کرنا واجب ہوگا چاہے سنے کا ارادہ کرے یا نہ کرے نا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک سجدہ تلاوت سنت ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن عمر بن الـخـطـاب قرأ يوم الجمعة على المنبر بسورة النحل حتى اذا جاء السجدة نزل فسجد و سجد الناس حتى اذا كانت الجمعة القابلة قرأ بها حتى ! اذا جاء السجدة قال ايها الناس انما نمر بالسجود فمن سجد فقد اصاب ومن لم يسجد فلا اثم عليه ولم يسجد عمر ) () (بخاری شریف، باب من و ای ان الله عز وجل لم یوجب السجودص ۱۴۷ نمبر ۷ ۱۰۷ را ابو داؤد شریف ، باب السجودنی ص ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۱۴۱۰ار ترمندی شریف ، باب ما جاء من لم يسجد فیہ ص ۱۲۷ نمبر ۵۷۶) اس حدیث واثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ تلاوت واجب نہیں ہے سنت ہے۔ سجدہ کرے گا تو ثواب ملے گا اور نہیں کرے گا تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ بعض حضرات کا مذہب یہ بھی ہے کہ سننے کے ارادے سے سنے تو سجدہ کرے گا اور اگر بغیر ارادہ کے سن لیا تو اس پر ضروری نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے قال سلمان ما لهذا غدونا وقال عثمان انما السجدة على من استمعها (ه) ( بخاری شریف، باب من رأی ان اللہ عزوجل یا جب السجود ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۱۰۷۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سننے کے حاشیہ : (الف) ابن عباس نے فرمایا کہ سورہ صر میں تاکیدی سجدہ نہیں ہے پھر بھی حضور کو دیکھا کہ اس میں سجدہ کیا کرتے تھے (ب) حضور آیت سجدہ پڑھتے اور ہم ان کے پاس ہوتے تو آپ سجدہ کرتے اور ہم لوگ بھی آپ کے ساتھ سجدہ کرتے تو ہم لوگ بھیڑ کر دیتے۔ یہاں تک کہ ہم میں سے بعض پیشانی رکھنے کی جگہ نہیں پاتے کہ اس پر سجدہ کرے (ج) سعید بن جبیر فرماتے ہیں کہ جو آیت سجدہ سنے اس پر یہ ہے کہ سجدہ کرے (د) عمر ابن خطاب نے جمعہ کے دن منبر پر سورۃ النحل پڑھی یہاں تک کہ جب آیت سجدہ آئی تو نیچے اترے اور سجدہ کیا۔ اور لوگوں نے بھی سجدہ کیا یہاں تک کہ جب اگلا جمعہ آیا تو اس کو پڑھا یہاں تک کہ جب آیت سجدہ آئی تو کہا اے لوگو! ہم سجدہ پر گزرتے ہیں تو جس نے سجدہ کیا اس نے ٹھیک کیا اور جس نے سجدہ نہیں کیا اس پر کوئی گناہ نہیں ہے۔ اور حضرت عمر نے سجدہ نہیں کیا (7) حضرت سلمان نے فرمایا ہم اس سجدہ کے لئے نہیں آتے ہیں ، حضرت عثمان نے فرمایا سجد اس پر ہے جو سجدہ کو کان لگا کر سنے۔
[320] (2) Prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter and the listener, whether he intended to hear the Quran or not. Upon reciting these verses, prostration becomes obligatory on both the reciter and the listener, whether he intended to listen or not. The evidence for it being obligatory is this athar: from Ibn Abbas: he said regarding Surah Sad: it is not among the binding prostrations, yet I saw the Prophet (saw) prostrate in it. Footnote (a): He prostrated in Surah al-Najm, and with him prostrated the Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans. (b) Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and al-Hasan said that in Surah al-Hajj there is one sajda, the first of them. (c) Ibn Abbas said: in Surah al-Hajj, the first is emphatic (takidi) and the second is for teaching (ta'lim), and he would not prostrate in it. (d) I said to the Prophet (saw): In Surah al-Hajj there are two sajdas? He said: Yes, and whoever does not prostrate them, then he does not recite them. And prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter and the listener, whether he intended to hear the Quran or not. (a) (Bukhari, chapter on prostration in Sad, p. 146 no. 1069; Abu Dawood, chapter on prostration in Sad, p. 307 no. 1409; Tirmidhi, chapter on what came about prostration in Sad, p. 127 no. 577). From this hadith it is known that the prostration in Surah Sad is not emphatic. Its opposite meaning (mafhum mukhalif) is that the prostration of other verses is emphatic, and its name is obligation (wujub). Therefore sujud al-tilawah is wajib. Another hadith gives an indication: from Ibn Umar: he said: The Prophet (saw) would recite a sajda verse while we were with him, so he would prostrate and we would prostrate with him, and we would crowd so much that one of us could not find a place for his forehead to prostrate upon. (b) (Bukhari, chapter on crowding of people when the imam recites the sajda, p. 146 no. 1076; Muslim, chapter on sujud al-tilawah, p. 215 no. 575). This hadith indicates that prostration is obligatory and also obligatory on the listeners. For this reason, after hearing, all the people would prostrate until no space remained for prostration. From this hadith it is also known that even if one did not intend to hear the sajda verse, prostration becomes obligatory upon hearing it, because among those people there would be many who did not intend to listen, yet they still prostrated. (2) This athar supports it: from Ibn Umar: he said: Prostration is only upon those who hear it. Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: Whoever hears the sajda verse must prostrate. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, p. 207, no. 4222/4225). From this athar it is known that whoever hears the sajda verse must prostrate, whether he intended to listen or not. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, sujud al-tilawah is sunnah. His evidence is this athar: from Umar ibn al-Khattab: he recited Surah al-Nahl on the pulpit on Friday until when he came to the sajda verse, he descended and prostrated, and the people prostrated. Then on the following Friday, he recited it until when he came to the sajda verse, he said: O people, we pass by prostrations, so whoever prostrates has done well, and whoever does not prostrate, there is no sin on him. And Umar did not prostrate. (Bukhari, chapter on whoever saw that Allah did not make prostration obligatory, p. 147 no. 1077; Abu Dawood, chapter on prostration in Sad, p. 207 no. 1410; Tirmidhi, chapter on what came about the one who does not prostrate, p. 127 no. 576). From this hadith and athar it is known that sujud al-tilawah is not wajib but sunnah. If one prostrates, he gets reward; if he does not, there is no sin. Some people also hold the view that if one listens with intent to hear, then he should prostrate; but if he hears without intent, it is not necessary. Their evidence is this athar: Salman said: We did not come out for this. And Uthman said: Prostration is only upon the one who listens attentively (istama'a). (Bukhari, chapter on whoever saw that Allah did not make prostration obligatory, p. 146 no. 1077). From this athar it is known that... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the legal ruling of sujud al-tilawah: whether it is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah (recommended). The Hanafi school holds it to be wajib on both the reciter and the listener, regardless of whether the listener intended to hear the Quran or not. The evidence includes: (1) the hadith of Ibn Abbas about Surah Sad, where the Prophet prostrated even though it is not among the mu'azamat (binding prostrations) — by mafhum mukhalif, other sajdas are binding; (2) the hadith of Ibn Umar showing that the companions would prostrate even if crowded, implying obligation; (3) the athar of Ibn Umar and Sa'id ibn Jubayr that prostration is upon the one who hears. The Shafi'i school considers it sunnah, citing the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab who, in one Friday, prostrated, and in another, did not and stated that there is no sin on the one who does not prostrate. Additionally, there is a view that it is only required if one listens with intent, based on the statements of Salman and Uthman. The text presents both sides, but the Hanafi position is supported with stronger evidence from the apparent meaning of hadith.

Key Terms
سجدہ تلاوت (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a sajda verse of the Quran.
تالی (tali): The one who recites the sajda verse.
سامع (sami'): The one who hears the sajda verse, whether intentionally or unintentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, on whom is sujud al-tilawah wajib?
A) Only on the reciter
B) On both the reciter and the listener, regardless of intent
C) Only on the listener who intended to hear
D) Only on the one who recites or hears in a mosque

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sujud al-tilawah is wajib on both the reciter and the listener, regardless of intent, based on the practice of the Prophet and companions.

Salah — Prayer

The Ruling of Sajda Tilawa: Wajib or Sunnah?
Presents Hanafi proofs for wajib sajda tilawa and the Shafi'i counter-evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sajda tilawa, identify the key proofs, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Sajda tilawa is wajib upon reciter and listener – the Prophet's practice and companion rulings confirm it.

This lesson examines the ruling of sajda tilawa (prostration of recitation) in the Hanafi school and the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'is. The Hanafi school holds it as wajib based on explicit hadith and practice of the Prophet (PBUH) and companions. The Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. Understanding the proofs and the practical difference is essential for accurate fiqh knowledge.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: sajda tilawa is wajib upon both the reciter and the listener, regardless of intention.
Wajib in Hanafi terminology means obligatory but with a lesser degree of certainty than fard.
2
Identify the Hanafi proofs
Locate the hadith of Ibn Umar about crowding during sajda, and the athar of Ibn Umar and Sa'id ibn Jubayr stating that prostration is upon the hearer.
The hadith shows that the Prophet and companions always prostrated, even if crowded.
3
Identify the opposing Shafi'i proof
Find the narration from Umar ibn al-Khattab where he did not prostrate on a Friday sermon and said there is no sin in omitting it.
Shafi'is use this as evidence that sajda is not obligatory.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is implicit: the consistent practice of the Prophet and the explicit statements of Ibn Umar and Sa'id ibn Jubayr are stronger evidence. Umar's action may have been a concession to avoid burdening the congregation.
This is a methodological difference in how each school weighs evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi must prostrate when reciting or hearing a sajda verse, even unintentionally; a Shafi'i may omit it without sin.
This difference affects daily worship, especially during Quran recitation and listening.

Book of Prayer. And prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter and the listener, whether he intended to hear the Quran or not. (a) (Bukhari, chapter of prostration, p. 146 no. 1069/Abu Dawud, chapter of prostration, p. 307 no. 1409/Tirmidhi, chapter of prostration, p. 127 no. 577). From this hadith it is known that in Surah Sad, the prostration is not emphatic. Its opposite meaning is that the prostration of other verses is emphatic and its name is obligation. Therefore sajda tilawa is wajib. Another hadith gives an indication: from Ibn Umar, he said: The Prophet used to recite a verse of sajda while we were with him, so he would prostrate and we would prostrate with him, and we crowded so much that one of us could not find a place for his forehead to prostrate on. (b) (Bukhari, chapter of crowding when the imam recites the sajda, p. 146 no. 1076 and Muslim, chapter of sajda of Quran, p. 215 no. 575). From this hadith it is known that prostration is wajib and also wajib upon the listeners. For this reason, after hearing, all people used to prostrate, until no space remained for prostration. From this hadith it is also known that even if one does not intend to hear the verse of sajda, by hearing it the prostration becomes wajib, because among the many people there were those who did not intend to hear, yet they prostrated. (2) This effect supports: from Ibn Umar, he said: Prostration is only upon the one who hears it. Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: Whoever hears the verse of sajda, upon him is to prostrate. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 207, chapter of those who say prostration is upon the one who sits for it and the one who hears it, vol. 1 p. 367, nos. 4222/4225). From this effect it is known that whoever hears the verse of sajda, prostration becomes wajib upon him, whether he intended to hear or not. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, sajda tilawa is sunnah. Their proof is this effect: from Umar ibn al-Khattab: He recited Surah an-Nahl on the pulpit on Friday, and when he came to the verse of sajda, he descended and prostrated, and the people prostrated. Until the next Friday, he recited it, and when he came to the verse of sajda, he said: O people, we only pass by prostration; whoever prostrates has done rightly, and whoever does not prostrate has no sin. And Umar did not prostrate. () (Bukhari, chapter of those who see that Allah did not make prostration obligatory, p. 147 no. 1077; Abu Dawud, chapter of prostration, p. 207 no. 1410; Tirmidhi, chapter of one who does not prostrate in it, p. 127 no. 576). From this hadith and effect it is known that sajda tilawa is not wajib, it is sunnah. If one prostrates, he gets reward; if he does not, there is no harm. Some people also hold that if one hears with intention, he prostrates; if he hears without intention, it is not necessary. Their proof is this effect: Salman said: We did not come for this prostration; Uthman said: Prostration is only upon the one who listens attentively. (e) (Bukhari, chapter of those who see that Allah did not make prostration obligatory, p. 146 no. 1077). From this effect it is known that listening with intention... Footnote: (a) Ibn Abbas said that in Surah Sad there is no emphatic prostration, yet he saw the Prophet prostrating in it. (b) The Prophet would recite the verse of sajda and we were with him, then he would prostrate and we would prostrate with him, and we would crowd so that some of us could not find a place to place his forehead. (c) Sa'id ibn Jubayr says: Whoever hears the verse of sajda, upon him is to prostrate. (d) Umar ibn al-Khattab recited Surah an-Nahl on the pulpit on Friday, and when he came to the verse of sajda, he descended and prostrated, and the people prostrated. When the next Friday came, he recited it, and when he came to the verse of sajda, he said: O people, we only pass by prostration; whoever prostrates has done rightly, and whoever does not prostrate has no sin. And Umar did not prostrate. (7) Salman said: We did not come for this prostration; Uthman said: Prostration is only upon the one who listens with his ear.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over the ruling of sajda tilawa (prostration of recitation). The author presents the Hanafi position that it is wajib, citing several hadith and athar. The first hadith (from Surah Sad) is used to derive that prostration in other surahs is emphatic (wajib). Then the hadith of Ibn Umar about crowding shows that the Prophet and companions prostrated upon hearing, indicating obligation even for listeners. The athar from Ibn Umar and Sa'id ibn Jubayr explicitly state that prostration is upon the one who hears. Then the Shafi'i position is presented: sajda tilawa is sunnah, based on Umar's action and statement where he did not prostrate and said there is no sin in omitting it. A third view is also mentioned: it is only necessary if one intended to listen, based on the statement of Salman and Uthman. The author does not explicitly refute the opposing arguments here but presents them as part of the commentary. The Hanafi reliance on the hadith of Ibn Umar and the athar of the Companions establishes wajib as the stronger position.

Key Terms
سجدہ تلاوت (sajda tilawa): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission is sinful but not to the level of fard in evidence.
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act whose performance brings reward and omission does not incur sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sajda tilawa is wajib in the Hanafi school upon the reciter and listener, with intention not being a condition.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Sajda Tilawa in Congregational Prayer: Three Key Scenarios
Rulings on sajda tilawa in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sajda tilawa when the imam recites, when the follower recites, and when a verse is heard from outside the prayer, and apply the principle of the imam as guarantor (damir).

Core Idea
The imam's recitation obligates both; the follower's recitation obligates none because he should not recite.

Sajda tilawa is a wajib act when one recites or hears a verse of prostration. In congregational prayer, the ruling varies depending on who recites and the context. This lesson covers three specific scenarios derived from the matn and its commentary, supported by hadith and the principle of the imam being a guarantor (damir) for the follower's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage explicitly states three cases: (1) imam recites, (2) follower recites, (3) a verse is heard from someone outside the current prayer. Note the ruling for each.
2
Analyze the ruling for imam reciting
When the imam recites a sajda verse, both imam and follower must prostrate. The commentary invokes the hadith where the Prophet prostrated and companions followed, and the principle that the imam is a guarantor (damir) – his actions encompass the follower.
Proof: Hadith in Bukhari and the damir concept.
3
Analyze the ruling for follower reciting
If the follower recites a sajda verse, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate. The reasoning: the follower should not be reciting at all (according to Abu Hanifa), and even if he does, he cannot introduce an action that opposes the imam.
This underscores the subordinate role of the follower (iqtida).
4
Analyze the ruling for hearing from outside
If those in prayer hear a sajda verse from someone not in that prayer, they must not prostrate during the prayer; they should prostrate after finishing. If they do prostrate during prayer, it is not sufficient for the sajda tilawa but does not invalidate the prayer.
The cause is external, so prostration is deferred. Supported by the athar of Tawus.
5
Synthesize the underlying principles
Three principles tie these rulings: (a) The imam's recitation includes the follower (damir). (b) The follower must not act independently in recitation or prostration. (c) Actions not part of the prayer's structure (like sajda tilawa from an external cause) should not be performed during prayer to avoid disruption.
These principles ensure the unity and order of congregational prayer.

Source Text

فاذا تلا الامام آية السجدة سجدها و سجد الماموم معه [۳۲۲](۴) فان تلا الماموم لم يلزم الامام ولا الماموم السجود ۳۲۳) (۵) وان سمعوا وهم في الصلوة آية سجدة من رجل ليس معهم فى الصلوة لم يسجدوها في الصلوة فان سجدوها في الصلوة لم تجز لهم ولم تفسد صلوتهم.

If the imam recites a verse of sajda, he prostrates and the follower prostrates with him. (4) If the follower recites, neither the imam nor the follower are obligated to prostrate. (5) If they hear a verse of sajda while in prayer from a man who is not with them in prayer, they do not prostrate for it in the prayer. If they prostrate for it in the prayer, it is not sufficient and does not invalidate their prayer. (321) (3) So if the imam recited a verse of sajda, he will prostrate and the follower will also prostrate with him. (1) It has passed earlier that the imam is a guarantor (damir), so when the imam is obligated, the follower is also obligated. (2) The proof for this is also that in issue no. 2 there is: The Prophet used to recite the verse of sajda while we were with him, so he prostrates and we prostrate with him. (a) (Bukhari, chapter of crowding of people, p. 146 no. 1076). In this hadith, the Prophet prostrated and we also prostrated under his leadership. (322) (4) So if the follower recited a verse of sajda, neither the imam nor the follower are obligated to prostrate. The follower is subordinate to the imam; therefore if the follower recited the verse of sajda, the imam is not obligated to prostrate due to that. And the follower cannot oppose the imam by prostrating, nor would opposition be necessary, so neither the imam nor the follower are obligated. (2) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the follower should not recite at all; what he recited is against the rule, so no one is obligated to prostrate. [323] (5) If people are in prayer and they heard a verse of sajda from a man who is not with them in prayer, then they should not prostrate for it in the prayer. And if they prostrate for it in the prayer, it is not sufficient but their prayer is not invalidated. Some people were praying; a man not in that prayer recited a verse of sajda and the praying people heard it. So the praying people should not prostrate immediately but should prostrate after finishing the prayer. But if they prostrated in the prayer, the prayer is not invalid. This prostration is not part of the prayer actions; its cause came from outside the prayer, so it should not be performed in the prayer; it should be performed outside. However, if they did it, since it is not contradictory to prayer, the prayer is not invalidated. (2) This effect supports: from Tawus concerning a man who hears the sajda while in prayer: he said, 'Do not prostrate.' (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 216, chapter of one who hears the sajda recited while in prayer: those who say do not prostrate, vol. 1 p. 1374, no. 4303). In this chapter there are several effects; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter when you hear the sajda while praying, vol. 3... Footnote: (a) You recited the verse of sajda and we were with him, so he prostrated and we prostrated with him. (b) A narration from Tawus about a man who heard a verse of sajda while in prayer: he said, 'He should not prostrate.'
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed rulings for sajda tilawa in the context of congregational prayer. The matn states three cases: (3) If the imam recites, both imam and follower prostrate. The commentary explains the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet prostrated and companions followed. The principle of the imam being 'damir' (guarantor) is invoked: the imam's recitation includes the follower. (4) If the follower recites, neither is obligated. The reasoning is that the follower is subordinate and should not be reciting at all in the Hanafi view; thus no obligation. (5) If during prayer they hear from someone outside the prayer, they should not prostrate in the prayer; if they do, it is not accepted for the sajda tilawa but does not invalidate the prayer. The commentary clarifies that the cause is external, so prostration should be after prayer, citing the athar of Tawus who advised not prostrating while in prayer. The rulings are based on the same hadith and the principle of avoiding disruption to the prayer.

Key Terms
ماموم (ma'mum): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind the imam.
ضامن (damir): The imam is considered a guarantor, meaning his recitation and actions include the follower.
اقتداء (iqtida): Following the imam in prayer; the follower's acts are linked to the imam's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prostrate immediately in your prayer
B) Do not prostrate and ignore it
C) Prostrate after completing your prayer
D) Signal the imam to prostrate

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi congregational prayer, only the imam's recitation of a sajda verse obligates immediate prostration; the follower's recitation does not, and hearing from outside requires post-prayer prostration.

Rulings on Sujud al-Tilawah in Prayer and Multiple Recitations
Six specific rulings on sujud al-tilawah in and out of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sujud al-tilawah across six distinct scenarios involving imam, follower, hearing from outside, and multiple recitations, and explain the underlying principle of tadakhul.

Core Idea
Imam's recitation obligates prostration; follower's does not; one prostration suffices for repeated verses in one sitting due to tadakhul.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri presents six specific cases on when sujud al-tilawah is required or not, both in and out of prayer. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly performing the prostration in various contexts, especially regarding the roles of imam and follower and the handling of multiple recitations. The text is supported by hadith and athar from the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Extract the ruling for each scenario
Identify the six distinct cases (3-8) from the passage. For each, write a one-line ruling statement.
Cases: (3) imam recites → imam and follower prostrate; (4) follower recites → no one prostrates; (5) hear from outside → no prostration in prayer, but later; (6) recites outside then in prayer → one prostration suffices; (7) prostrates outside then recites in prayer → must prostrate again; (8) repeats verse in one sitting → one prostration suffices.
2
Identify the key condition that changes the ruling
For each scenario, note the condition (e.g., reciter is imam vs follower, in prayer vs outside, same sitting vs different). This condition is the 'illa' that determines the hukm.
For example, the imam's authority triggers obligation; the follower's improper recitation waives it; the location (in prayer vs out) affects sufficiency of prostration.
3
Map each ruling to its proof (dalil) from the footnotes
Match the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) and the athar from Tawus, Mujahid, Ibrahim, and Abu Abd al-Rahman to the applicable rulings.
The Bukhari hadith supports ruling 3. Tawus supports ruling 5. Mujahid and Ibrahim support ruling 6 and 8. Abu Abd al-Rahman supports ruling 8.
4
Explain the reasoning behind tadakhul in rulings 6 and 8
Analyze why one prostration suffices for multiple recitations (tadakhul) due to hardship (haraj). Note that ruling 7 is an exception because the earlier prostration is inferior.
In prayer, the prostration is more complete, so it covers the outside recitation (6). But inferior outside prostration cannot cover the prayer (7).
5
Note the ikhtilaf with other schools
Identify where the Hanafi school differs from others, particularly on the follower's recitation (ruling 4). State the opposing view and the practical consequence.
Shafi'i holds the follower must prostrate when reciting; Hanafi does not. The thamarah: in practice, a Hanafi follower does not prostrate, while a Shafi'i follower does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
(۳) فاذا تلا الامام آية السجدة سجدها و سجد الماموم معه (۴) فان تلا الماموم لم يلزم الامام ولا الماموم السجود (۵) وان سمعوا وهم في الصلوة آية سجدة من رجل ليس معهم فى الصلوة لم يسجدوها في الصلوة فان سجدوها في الصلوة لم تجز لهم ولم تفسد صلوتهم.
(۶) و من تلا آية سجدة خارج الصلوة ولم يسجدها حتى دخل في الصلوة فتلاها وسجد لهما اجزأته السجدة عن التلاوتين (۷) فان تلاها في غير الصلوة فسجدها ثم دخل فى الصلوة فتلاها سجدها ثانيا ولم تجزه السجدة الاولى (۸) ومن كرر تلاوة سجدة واحدة في مجلس واحد اجزأته سجدة واحدة.
حاشیہ : (الف) كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقرأ السجدة ونحن عنده فيسجد ونسجد معه (بخاری شریف)
عن طاؤس في الرجل سمع السجدة وهو في الصلوة قال لا يسجد (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة)
عن مجاهد قال اذا قرأت السجدة اجزاك ان تسجد بها مرة، عن ابراهيم في الرجل يقرأ السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها قال تجزيها السجدة الأولى (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة)
عن ابی عبد الرحمن انه كان يقرأ السجدة فيسجد ثم يعيدها في مجلسه ذلك مرارا لا يسجد (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة)
Book of Prayer. (3) So if the imam recites a verse of prostration, he prostrates for it and the follower prostrates with him. (4) If the follower recites, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate. (5) If they hear a verse of prostration while they are in prayer from a man who is not with them in the prayer, they do not prostrate for it in the prayer; if they prostrate for it in the prayer, it does not suffice for them and their prayer is not invalidated. (6) Whoever recites a verse of prostration outside the prayer and does not prostrate for it until he enters the prayer, then recites it and prostrates for both, the prostration suffices for both recitations. (7) If he recites it outside the prayer and prostrates for it, then enters the prayer and recites it, he prostrates for it a second time and the first prostration does not suffice for him. (8) Whoever repeats one prostration verse in one sitting, one prostration suffices for him. Footnote: (a) The Prophet (PBUH) used to recite a prostration verse while we were with him, so he would prostrate and we would prostrate with him (Bukhari). From Tawus regarding a man who hears a prostration verse while in prayer: he said, 'He does not prostrate' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). From Mujahid: he said, 'When you recite a prostration verse, one prostration suffices you'; from Ibrahim regarding a man who recites a prostration verse then repeats its recitation: he said, 'The first prostration suffices for it' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). From Abu Abd al-Rahman: he used to recite a prostration verse and prostrate, then repeat it in that same sitting many times without prostrating again (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah).
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri is a commentary on a matn (likely al-Quduri) containing rulings on Sujud al-Tilawah. The author presents six distinct cases. The first ruling (3) establishes that when the imam recites an ayah of sajdah in prayer, both he and the followers must prostrate. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) recorded in Bukhari, where the Prophet would recite and prostrate and the companions prostrated with him. The second ruling (4) states that if a follower recites an ayah of sajdah, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate. The logic given in the Urdu commentary is that the follower should not recite at all in prayer according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and since his recitation is against the rule, it imposes no obligation. The third ruling (5) covers the case where praying individuals hear an ayah of sajdah from someone not in their prayer. They should not prostrate during the prayer; instead, they must prostrate after completing the prayer. If they do prostrate during the prayer, it does not count for the sajdah, but their prayer remains valid. This is supported by the athar from Tawus. The fourth ruling (6) addresses the scenario of a person who recites an ayah of sajdah outside prayer, delays the prostration, then recites it again within the prayer in the same sitting. One prostration in the prayer suffices for both recitations because the prayer prostration is superior and includes the lesser one. The fifth ruling (7) adds the reverse: if a person prostrates outside prayer for a verse, then enters prayer and recites the same verse, the earlier prostration does not suffice; he must prostrate again. This is because the outside prostration is inferior and cannot cover the prayer prostration. The sixth ruling (8) states that if one repeats the same prostration verse multiple times in one sitting, a single prostration is sufficient. This is based on the principle of tadakhul (overlapping of causes) due to difficulty (haraj), as explained in the commentary. The athar from Ibrahim and Abu Abd al-Rahman confirm this. Overall, these rulings highlight the importance of the imam's role, the follower's subordination, and the rules governing multiple prostrations in and out of prayer.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran containing a command to prostrate.
تداخل (tadakhul): The principle that one act of prostration suffices for multiple recitations when in the same sitting due to difficulty in repeating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muqtadi (follower) recites an ayah of sajdah during prayer, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Both imam and muqtadi must prostrate.
B) Only the muqtadi must prostrate.
C) Neither the imam nor the muqtadi is obligated to prostrate.
D) The muqtadi must prostrate and repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The imam's recitation obligates prostration for all; the follower's recitation does not; and one prostration suffices for repeated recitations in the same sitting.

One Sajda for Multiple Tilawat in One Session
Ruling with proof on sufficiency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that one sajdat al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations in a single continuous session and explain the proof from the athar.

Core Idea
A single sajdat al-tilawah in prayer suffices for prior recitations in the same continuous session.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: you recite a prostration verse outside prayer, do not prostrate, then enter prayer and recite it again. Must you prostrate twice? The Hanafi school, relying on early authorities, rules that one prostration covers both – provided the session is uninterrupted. We will unpack the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the act under discussion (reciting a prostration verse) and the ruling (one sajda suffices for multiple recitations in one session).
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites two athar: from Mujahid and Ibrahim. Identify these as the evidence.
These are from the Musannaf of Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the athar prove the ruling: the explicit statement 'ajzāka an tasjuda bihā marrah' indicates sufficiency.
The word 'ajzā' implies legal adequacy.
4
Note the Hanafi Reasoning
The commentary adds two reasons: the prayer prostration is higher (ashraf) and thus suffices for the lower, and the session (majlis) is one.
5
Evaluate the Practical Scope
Consider when this ruling applies: continuous session, whether both recitations are outside prayer or one inside and one outside.
The ruling does not apply if the session is interrupted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Whoever recites a prostration verse outside prayer and did not prostrate until he entered prayer and recited it and prostrated for both, one prostration suffices him for the two recitations. (Commentary: The prayer prostration is higher, so it suffices for the lower. And because the session is one, one prostration in prayer suffices. Evidence: from Mujahid: 'When you recite the prostration, one prostration suffices you'; from Ibrahim concerning a man who recites the prostration then repeats its recitation: 'The first prostration suffices him.')
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage states a ruling and provides its proof. The ruling is: if a person recites a prostration verse outside prayer without prostrating, then enters prayer and recites the same verse and prostrates once, that single prostration counts for both recitations. The reason is that the prostration performed in prayer is of a higher rank (due to the sacred context and additional requirements) and thus suffices for the earlier one performed outside prayer. Additionally, the session (majlis) is considered one continuous occasion. The proof is an athar from Mujahid and Ibrahim confirming that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations in the same session.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
مجلس (majlis): A single sitting or session; continuity of time and place without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two prostrations: one for the outside recitation and one for the inside recitation.
B) One prostration is sufficient for both, provided the session is continuous.
C) No prostration is required because the first recitation was not acted upon immediately.
D) The prostration in prayer is invalid for the outside recitation; thus two are needed.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one sajdat al-tilawah performed in a continuous session suffices for all prostration recitations in that session.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Lower Prostration Cannot Substitute for Higher
Ruling on separate prostrations for same verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajda tilawa performed outside prayer and explain why it does not fulfill the obligation when the verse is recited inside prayer.

Core Idea
A lower-ranked act (outside prayer) cannot substitute for a higher-ranked obligation (inside prayer).

This lesson clarifies an important distinction in the obligation of sajda tilawa. The Hanafi school holds that the context of prostration matters: a prostration performed outside prayer is considered of lower rank ('adnā'), while one performed inside prayer is higher ('a‘lā'). Consequently, if you have already prostrated for a verse outside prayer, that does not exempt you from prostrating again if you recite the same verse inside prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine the specific act: sajda tilawa (prostration for recitation) both outside and inside prayer. The ruling is that sajda tilawa is wajib in both contexts according to Hanafi school.
Wajib means obligatory, but not at the level of fard.
2
Understand the Principle of Hierarchy
Grasp the legal principle that acts of worship have different ranks. A lower-ranked act (e.g., outer prostration) cannot fulfill a higher-ranked obligation (inner prostration). This is a general Hanafi rule derived from the sunnah and qiyas.
The terms 'adnā' and 'a‘lā' are key: one is lesser, the other greater.
3
Apply the Principle to the Given Scenario
If a person recites a sajda verse outside prayer, prostrates, then later enters prayer and recites the same verse, the first prostration does not count for the second. A new prostration inside prayer is required.
The act is repeated despite the same verse because the context changed the rank of the obligation.
4
Note Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider sajda tilawa as sunnah, not wajib, and might allow one prostration with general intention to cover all recitations. In Hanafi, however, the distinction is strict.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi must repeat the sajda inside prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲۵) (۷) فان تلاها في غير الصلوة فسجدها ثم دخل فى الصلوة فتلاها سجدها ثانيا ولم تجزه السجدة الاولى . (۱) نماز سے باہر والا سجدہ ادنی ہے اور نماز کے اندر کا سجدہ اعلی ہے۔ اس لئے ادنی والا سجدہ اعلی کے لئے کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے نماز سے باہر جو سجدہ کر چکا ہے وہ نماز کے اندر والے کے لئے کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ نماز کے اندر آیت سجدہ پڑھنے کی وجہ سے دوبارہ سجدہ کرنا ہوگا۔
If he recites it outside prayer and prostrates for it, then enters prayer and recites it, he prostrates it a second time, and the first prostration does not suffice him. (Commentary: The prostration outside prayer is lower, and the prostration inside prayer is higher. Therefore the lower prostration does not suffice for the higher. So the prostration done outside does not count for the one inside; a new prostration is required upon reciting inside prayer.)
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling that is the inverse of the previous one. If a person performs the prostration outside prayer before entering prayer, then later recites the same verse inside prayer, the earlier prostration does not count. The reasoning is that a lower act (outside prayer) cannot replace a higher one (inside prayer). Thus a new prostration is obligatory inside prayer. The proof is implied by the general principle that a lesser act does not fulfill a greater obligation.

Key Terms
ادنی (adnā): Of lower status or rank; here, prostration outside prayer.
اعلی (a‘lā): Of higher status or rank; prostration inside prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No additional prostration is needed; the first one suffices.
B) A new prostration inside prayer is required because the first was lower in rank.
C) He must repeat the prostration outside prayer with intention for prayer.
D) He must combine both prostrations into one by intention.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a lower-ranked prostration (outside prayer) cannot substitute for a higher-ranked one (inside prayer); a new sajda is wajib when the verse is recited in prayer.

One Sajda Tilawa for Repeated Recitation in One Session
Ruling on repetition of same prostration verse in one sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeated recitation of a prostration verse in one session and explain the istihsan basis for tadakhul.

Core Idea
Repeated recitation of a sajda verse in one session: one prostration suffices due to tadakhul to prevent hardship.

The default qiyas would require a separate prostration for each recitation of a prostration verse. However, Hanafi fiqh applies istihsan (juristic preference) to permit merging multiple obligatory prostrations into one when the recitations occur in the same session. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the rationale of tadakhul, the condition of a single majlis, and the prophetic practice that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is reciting a prostration verse multiple times. The Hanafi ruling: one sajda suffices for all recitations in one session.
The key term is 'tadakhul' (merging).
2
Understand the qiyas baseline
Qiyas would demand a separate sajda for each recitation because each recitation is an independent cause. Recognize this as the default analogy.
Qiyas here is strict; it assumes each cause obligates its own act.
3
Recognize the istihsan exception
The Hanafi school departs from qiyas using istihsan, based on the principle of removing hardship (raf‘ al-haraj). Tadakhul applies because the multiple recitations share the same cause and same session.
The illa (effective cause) for tadakhul is unity of session.
4
Note the condition of majlis
The ruling is conditional on the session being one. If the session changes (e.g., a new sitting or after a significant break), separate prostrations are required.
The lower (minor) is subsumed into the higher (major), but not vice versa.
5
Examine the proof
The passage cites an athar from Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami: he would recite a sajda verse, prostrate, then repeat it in the same session multiple times without prostrating again.
This Companion practice (qawl sahabi) is a valid proof in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۶] (۸) ومن كرر تلاوة سجدة واحدة في مجلس واحد اجزأته سجدة واحدة. وجه قیاس کے اعتبار سے ہر آیت پڑھنے کے لئے الگ الگ سجدہ واجب ہونا چاہئے۔ لیکن حرج کے لئے تداخل کر دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اس میں شرط یہ ہے کہ مجلس ایک ہو۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ادنی اعلی میں داخل ہو گا لیکن اعلی اونی میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ اب اوپر کی صورت میں ایک ہی آیت کئی مرتبہ پڑھی ہے تو اگر مجلس ایک ہے تو تداخل ہو کر ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور مجلس بدل گئی تو کئی سجدے لازم ہو نگے ۔(۲) اثر میں موجود ہے عن ابی عبد الرحمن انه كان يقرأ السجدة فيسجد ثم يعيدها في مجلسه ذلك مرارا لا يسجد (الف) مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۰۴، باب الرجل يقرأ السجدة ثم يعيد قرآتھا کیف یصنع ، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۶، نمبر ۴۲۰ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مجلس میں کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھا تو تداخل ہوگا اور ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔
Whoever repeats the recitation of one prostration verse in one session, one prostration suffices him. Explanation: According to qiyas, each recitation should require a separate prostration, but for the sake of preventing hardship, tadakhul (merging) is applied. The condition is that the session is one. Also, the lower is subsumed into the higher, but the higher is not subsumed into the lower. So if the same verse is recited multiple times in one session, tadakhul occurs and one prostration is necessary. If the session changes, multiple prostrations are required. Evidence from Abu Abd al-Rahman: he would recite a prostration verse and prostrate, then repeat it in that same session many times without prostrating again.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage addresses repetition of the same prostration verse in one session. The default qiyas would require a separate prostration for each recitation. However, Hanafi fiqh applies istihsan (juristic preference) based on tadakhul (merging) to avoid hardship, provided the session (majlis) remains unchanged. If the session changes, separate prostrations are required. The commentary also reiterates the principle that a lower act can be subsumed into a higher one (as in lesson 1), but not vice versa. The proof is an athar from Abu Abd al-Rahman who practiced this.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadākhul): Merging of multiple obligations into one due to shared cause or session.
حرج (ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty; the basis for istihsan to relax the strict qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites the same prostration verse five times in one sitting, how many prostrations are required according to the Hanafi school?
A) Five prostrations, one for each recitation.
B) One prostration suffices for all five.
C) Two prostrations: one for the first and one for the last.
D) No prostration is required if he did not intend to prostrate.

Key Takeaway
One prostration of recitation suffices for multiple recitations of the same sajda verse in one session, due to the application of tadakhul (merging) based on istihsan.

Method of Sajdat al-Tilawa
Ritual description with naqli proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of sajdat al-tilawa and identify the athar evidence for each element.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawa: takbir, prostration, takbir – no tashahhud, no salam.

This passage explains the precise method for the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa). While it resembles a normal prostration in prayer, it has its own unique form: it begins and ends with takbir, and crucially, it does not include tashahhud or salam. The Hanafi school derives this from the actions of the Companions and successors, as recorded in the Musannaf of Ibn Abi Shayba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sajdat al-tilawa is wajib upon reciting or hearing a prostration verse. Determine that this is the legal classification from the text.
The text implies wajib by requiring wudu and providing strict procedure.
2
List the steps of the act
From the text: 1) Say takbir without raising hands. 2) Prostrate (one sajdah). 3) Say takbir while rising. That is all – no tashahhud, no salam.
Raising hands is not done.
3
Identify what is excluded
The text explicitly states there is no tashahhud and no salam. This distinguishes sajdat al-tilawa from the prostration within a full prayer.
4
Locate the dalil for each element
For takbir: the athar from Abdullah ibn Muslim shows his father said Allahu Akbar then prostrated. For absence of tashahhud/salam: athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr and al-Hasan show they did not say salam.
The text also cites an athar from Ibrahim for the requirement of wudu.
5
Determine the hukm level of each element
The takbir is wajib based on the evidence; omitting it makes the sajda disliked but valid (according to some). The prostration itself is rukn. Wudu is shart (condition).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Whoever intends to prostrate should say takbir and not raise his hands, prostrate, then say takbir and raise his head, and there is no tashahhud upon him nor salam. Evidence: from Abdullah ibn Muslim: 'My father, when he recited a prostration verse, said Allahu Akbar then prostrated.' This shows that one enters prostration with just takbir. Also from Sa'id ibn Jubayr: 'He would recite a prostration verse, then raise his head and not say salam.' Al-Hasan would lead us in the prostrations of the Quran and not say salam. This shows no tashahhud or salam. Sajdat al-tilawa is part of prayer, so wudu is necessary. Evidence from Ibrahim: 'When he hears it while not in wudu, let him perform wudu, then recite, then prostrate.'
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for sajdat al-tilawa: it begins with takbir (without raising hands), then prostration, then another takbir upon rising. No tashahhud or salam is required, distinguishing it from the prostration in prayer (sajdah of salat). The proofs are athar from the Companions and Tabi'un. Additionally, wudu is required because it is considered part of prayer (i.e., a form of worship requiring purity). The cut-off athar from Ibrahim emphasizes the need for wudu.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' to commence or transition in sajda.
وضو (wuḍū’): Ritual purification required for sajda because it is considered part of salah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Saying takbir after prostration

D) Prostrating once

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawa is a wajib act performed with takbir, prostration, and takbir, without tashahhud or salam, and requires wudu.
