مسجد عبد القيس بجوائى من البحرين (و) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الجمعۃ فی القرى والمدن ص ۱۲۲ نمبر ۱/۸۹۲ ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعۃ فی القری ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسجد عبد القیس میں مدینہ کے بعد پہلی مرتبہ جمعہ ہوا ہے جو بحرین میں تھی ۔ اگر گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ہوتا تو بحرین کے فتح سے پہلے کتنے گاؤں
Jumu'ah is not valid except in a large city with a congregational mosque or in the prayer ground of the city, and it is not permissible in villages. Important note: Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of the city, and the first time it was established in Madinah. Its proof is from the verse: 'O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade.' (Surah al-Jumu'ah 9) This verse proves Jumu'ah. (346) (1) Jumu'ah is not valid except in the congregational mosque of the city or in the 'id ground of the city, and it is not permissible in villages. Jumu'ah is derived from jama'ah (congregation), therefore this condition is that it be in the city's congregational mosque or the city's open space. By musalla is meant 'id ground or the outskirts of the city. 'Misr jami'' is another translation: in a large city, not in a village. And according to the Hanafis, Jumu'ah is not permissible in villages. (1) There is an athar from 'Ali: 'No Jumu'ah and no tashriq except in a large city (misr jami'). And he counted the cities as Basra, Kufa, Madinah, and Bahrain.' (Mussanaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Qura al-Sighar, vol. 3 p. 67 no. 5175 / Mussanaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 5059) From this athar it is known that Jumu'ah is permissible in a large city. (2) This is also supported by the fact that around Madinah there were many villages called 'Awali, and they did not pray Jumu'ah there; rather, the people came to Madinah and prayed in the Prophet's mosque. If Jumu'ah were permissible in villages, why would they not pray in 'Awali? Why would they endure the hardship of sun and dust to come to Madinah? There is a hadith from 'A'isha: 'The people used to take turns coming to Jumu'ah from their homes and from 'Awali, and they would come in dust and sweat.' (Bukhari, Bab min ayna tu'ti al-jumu'ah, p. 123 no. 902; Abu Dawud, Bab man tajibu 'alayhi al-jumu'ah, p. 158 no. 1055) From this hadith it is known that Jumu'ah was not held in the villages of 'Awali; only in a city like Madinah. (3) After Madinah, the first Jumu'ah was held in a fortress called Jawatha. There is a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah after the Jumu'ah in the mosque of the Messenger of Allah was in the mosque of 'Abd al-Qays at Jawatha in Bahrain.' (Bukhari, Bab al-jumu'ah fi al-qura wa al-mudun, p. 122 no. 1/892; Abu Dawud, Bab al-jumu'ah fi al-qura, p. 60 no. 1068) This hadith shows that the first Jumu'ah after Madinah was in the mosque of 'Abd al-Qays in Bahrain. If Jumu'ah were permissible in villages, then before the conquest of Bahrain, how many villages...
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Jumu'ah prayer by stating its essential condition: it is only valid in a large city (misr jami') or its designated prayer ground (musalla). It is not valid in villages. The author provides multiple proofs: first, the general obligation of Jumu'ah from the Quran; second, the athar from 'Ali restricting Jumu'ah to large cities; third, the practice of the people of Madinah's suburbs ('Awali) who came to Madinah for Jumu'ah rather than praying in their villages, indicating that Jumu'ah was not performed in villages; fourth, the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas about the first Jumu'ah after Madinah being in Jawatha, a fortress in Bahrain, which was a city. The Hanafi position is that Jumu'ah requires a settled urban population with a central mosque.

Key Terms
مصر جامع (miṣr jāmiʿ): A large city or major town with a central congregational mosque.
مصلى المصر (muṣallā al-miṣr): The prayer ground (musalla) of the city, often used for 'Id prayers.
قرى (qurā): Villages or small rural settlements that do not meet the criteria of a misr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, where is Jumu'ah prayer valid?
A) In any mosque or open area
B) Only in a large city's congregational mosque or its 'Id ground
C) In any village with at least 40 men
D) Only in Mecca and Madinah

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid in a large city (misr) or its musalla; this condition is proven by the athar of 'Ali and the practice of the Companions, and Hanafis do not permit Jumu'ah in villages.

Friday Prayer: City vs Village – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the validity of Friday prayer in villages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of Friday prayer (being in a misr jamai or its musalla), explain the Hanafi evidence from athar and practice, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Jawathi case.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is only valid in a large city with a ruler and qisas – a village lacks the necessary conditions.

This lesson addresses a fundamental dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can Friday prayer be held in a village? The matn states it is not valid except in a large city (misr jamai) or its musalla. The commentator expands the proof, citing athar from Ali and the practice of the Companions, and responds to the Shafi'i reliance on the first Friday in Jawathi. Understanding this difference clarifies the Hanafi methodology of using companion reports and the practice of the Salaf over certain ahadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its key terms
State the ruling from the matn: Friday prayer is not valid except in a misr jamai (large city) or its musalla (prayer ground). Define misr jamai as a city with a ruler, qisas, and contiguous houses. Define musalla as the 'idgah or open space of the city.
The Hanafi condition is not just any congregation; it requires a settlement with organized governance and proximity.
2
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the athar from Ali: 'No Friday or tashreeq except in a large city.' Also note the practice of the people of 'Awali who came to Madinah for Friday, proving Friday was not established in their villages.
The Hanafis prioritize companion athar and practice over isolated hadith when there is conflict.
3
Present the Shafi'i opposition and their dalil
The Shafi'i school argues that Friday is valid in any village with forty residents, citing the hadith that the first Friday after Madinah was in Jawathi, a village of Bahrain, and the hadith of Umm Abdullah making Friday obligatory on every village even with three people.
These hadith appear to support village Friday, so the Hanafis must respond.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that Jawathi was actually a fortress and a city, called 'village' in a general sense, as Makkah is called a village in the Quran. The hadith of Umm Abdullah is considered weak (da'if). Thus the stronger evidence is the athar from Ali and the practice of the Salaf.
This shows the Hanafi principle of takhsis: the term 'qarya' can apply to cities, so the apparent dalil is not decisive.
5
Determine the practical consequence and mufta bihi
In practice, Hanafis do not permit Friday in small villages even with a mosque; it requires a large town meeting the conditions. Shafi'is permit it in any village with forty. The mufta bihi today is the Hanafi position, allowing Friday in large towns but not villages.
The thamarah al-khilaf directly affects communities: a village congregation using a Shafi'i imam may be valid for Shafi'is but not for Hanafis.

كتاب الصلوة
جوانی کے بارے میں منقول ہے کہ وہ ایک قلعہ کا نام ہے اور وہاں شہر تھا۔ قائد امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ہے جہاں چالیس آدمی نماز پڑھنے والے ہوں ۔ ان کی دلیل ابو داؤد کی یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال ان اول جمعة جمعت في الاسلام بعد جمعة جمعت في مسجد رسول الله له بالمدينة لجمعة جمعت بجواثى قرية من قرى البحرين قال عثمان قرية من قرى عبد القيس (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة في القرى ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جوانی بحرین کے گاؤں کا نام ہے۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ بعض مرتبہ شہر کو بھی قری کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے مکہ مکرمہ کو قرآن نے قریہ کہا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ام عبد الله الدوسية قالت سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول الجمعة واجبة على اهل كل قرية وان لم يكونوا الا ثلاثة ورابعهم امامهم (ب) (دارقطنی ، باب الجمعۃ علی اہل القرية ج ثانی ص سے نمبر ۱۵۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گاؤں میں جمعہ واجب ہے (۲) عن ابي اما مة ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال على الخميس جمعة ليس فيما دون ذلك (دار قطنی ، ذکر العدد فی الجمعة ج خانی ص ۴ نمبر ۱۵۶۴ را ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة في القرى ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۹) مصر جامع کس کو کہتے ہیں اس کی تعریف اس اثر میں ہے قلت لعطاء ما القرية الجامعة قال ذات الجماعة والامير والقصاص والدور المجتمعة غير المفترقة الآخذ بعضها ببعض كهيئة جده (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ج ثالث ص ۶۸ نمبر ۵۱۷۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بڑی بستی اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں امیر ہو، قصاص اور حدود نافذ کئے جاتے ہوں اور گھر قریب قریب ہوں، خیمہ زنوں کی طرح دور دور گھر نہ ہوں۔ شہر کی دوسری تعریف یہ ہے سمـعـت عـمـر بن دينار يقول اذا كان المسجد يجمع فيه الصلوة فلتصل فيه الجمعة (و) مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القرى الصغارج ثالث ص ۷۰ انمبر ۵۱۸۴) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر تمام آدمی جمع ہو کر ایک مسجد میں نماز پڑھتے ہوں تو اس میں جمعہ جائز ہے۔
آج کل بڑی بستی میں جمعہ جائز ہونے کا فتوی دیتے ہیں۔
The Friday prayer is not valid except in a large city congregational mosque or in the prayer ground of the city, and it is not permissible in villages.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the validity of Friday prayer in villages. The Hanafi position, derived from the matn, is that Friday prayer is only valid in a large city (misr jamai) or its musalla (prayer ground), not in villages. The commentator begins by explaining the ruling: Friday prayer is obligatory on city dwellers, and its proof is the verse 'O you who believe, when the call for prayer on Friday is made, hasten to the remembrance of Allah...' (62:9). He then states the condition: the prayer must be in the central mosque of the city or its open space (fana al-misr). The musalla refers to the 'idgah or the city's periphery. The Hanafi school does not permit Friday prayer in villages. Evidence is cited from Ali (ra) that there is no Friday or tashreeq except in a large city. The practice of the people of 'Awali (suburbs of Madinah) is also given: they would come to Madinah for Friday prayer rather than praying in their villages, indicating that it was not established there. The first Friday after Madinah was in Jawathi, which was a fortress and a city, not a village. The Shafi'i view is then presented: Friday prayer is valid in villages with forty participants. Their evidence includes the hadith that the first Friday after Madinah was in Jawathi, a village of Bahrain. The Hanafi response is that sometimes a city is called a village, as Makkah is called a village in the Quran. Thus, Jawathi was a city. Another Shafi'i hadith is also weakened. Finally, the definition of 'misr jamai' is provided from Atha: a place with a ruler, where qisas is implemented, and houses are close together. Also, from Umar ibn Dinar: if the mosque gathers people for the five daily prayers, Friday can be observed there. The commentator concludes that today, Friday is permitted in large towns. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of using athar (companion reports), practice of the Salaf, and rational inference (istihsan) to defend their position against the Shafi'i school.

Key Terms
مصر جامع (misr jamai): A large city or capital with a ruler, where qisas is implemented, and houses are contiguous.
مصلى (musalla): The prayer ground (idgah) or open space of the city (fana al-misr).
تشريق (tashreeq): Refers to the Takbir al-Tashreeq recited after prayers on the days of Eid al-Adha; mentioned in the hadith of Ali along with jumu'ah.
قرى (qura): Villages; plural of qarya. In this context, settlements smaller than a misr jamai.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for the validity of Friday prayer regarding the location?
A) It can be performed in any village with at least 40 people.
B) It must be performed in a large city (misr jamai) or its musalla.
C) It can be performed anywhere as long as there is a pulpit.
D) It must be performed in the Prophet's Mosque in Madinah.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer in the Hanafi school is only valid in a large city (misr jamai) meeting specific conditions or its open space (musalla); village Friday is not accepted.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Ruler's Permission Required for Friday Prayer
Stating the condition that Friday prayer requires the ruler's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of Friday prayer and identify the authority required.

Core Idea
Friday prayer requires the ruler's permission — authority ensures order in large congregations.

This lesson examines a fundamental Hanafi ruling that Friday prayer is only valid when established by the ruler or his deputy. The matn states this condition clearly, and the commentary provides the rationale: large crowds need organized authority. Understanding this condition is key to applying the Hanafi position on congregational worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Condition
Recognize that the act is Friday prayer (salat al-Jumu'ah) and the condition is that it must be established by the ruler (sultan) or his appointed deputy.
The condition is a shart for validity.
2
State the Ruling in Arabic and English
The matn says: 'ولا تجوز اقامتها الا للسلطان او لمن امره السطان.' Translate and memorize this phrase.
Literally: 'And it is not permissible to establish it except for the ruler or for one whom the ruler has ordered.'
3
Understand the Rationale
The commentary explains that Friday prayer gathers many people; controlling them is not everyone's task. Therefore, authority is needed to maintain order.
This rationale is not part of the ruling itself but helps explain the wisdom.
4
Recognize the Evidence
The author cites an athar from Abdullah ibn Umar: when asked about villages between Makkah and Madinah, he confirmed Friday prayer is valid if a ruler is present.
This is a weak evidence according to some, but used as support for the Hanafi position.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not require the ruler's permission for Friday prayer. This is a valid ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۴۷] (۲) ولا تجوز اقامتها الا للسلطان او لمن امره السطان.
چونکہ جمعہ میں بہت لوگ ہوتے ہیں، ان کو سنبھالنا سب کا کام نہیں ہے اس لئے بادشاہ یا بادشاہ کا مامور جمعہ قائم کرے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے سال عبد الله بن عمر بن خطاب عن القرى التي بين مكة والمدينة ماترى في الجمعة قال نعم اذا كان
And it is not permissible to establish it (Friday prayer) except for the ruler or for one whom the ruler has ordered.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This is a brief ruling stating that Friday prayer can only be established by the ruler (sultan) or his appointed deputy. The commentator explains the wisdom: Friday prayer gathers large crowds, and organizing them is not everyone's job. Therefore, it must be conducted by the ruler or his agent. He also mentions an effect (athar) from Abdullah ibn Umar as evidence: when asked about villages between Makkah and Madinah, he said yes, Friday is valid if there is a ruler. This ruling underscores the importance of authority and order in congregational worship.

Key Terms
سلطان (sultan): The ruler or sovereign authority who has control over the city.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is permitted to establish Friday prayer according to this ruling?
A) Any adult male Muslim
B) The ruler or his appointed deputy
C) Any person who knows the Quran
D) The most pious person in the community

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the ruler's permission for Friday prayer as a condition of validity.

Salah — Prayer

Jumu'ah Requires Sultan or His Appointee
Ruling that Jumu'ah requires sultan or his appointee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of the sultan for Jumu'ah, outline the Shafi'i counter-proof, and explain the Hanafi response distinguishing between qarya and misr.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah needs a ruler with authority; mere forty residents are insufficient in the Hanafi school.

The Hanafi school holds that Jumu'ah (Friday congregational prayer) is only valid when established by the sultan or his appointed representative. This condition stems from the need for authority to manage the large gathering. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing hadith about Jumu'ah in villages. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: Jumu'ah is only permissible for the sultan or his appointee. Note the hukm level (wajib) and the condition attached.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that Jumu'ah is valid in any village with at least forty residents, regardless of a ruler's permission.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith about the first Jumu'ah at Jawatha (a village) and the hadith that Jumu'ah is obligatory on every village, even with three people.
Focus on the specific narrations cited in the passage.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the term 'qarya' in hadith can mean a town, not a mere village. They define 'qarya jami'a' as requiring a ruler, enforcement of penalties, and contiguous houses. Jawatha was actually a town. The hadith about three people is weak or interpreted differently.
Consider the athar of 'Ata and Ibn 'Umar that support the ruler condition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in a location without a sultan, Hanafi deem Jumu'ah not valid (must pray Zuhr), while Shafi'i consider it valid. Modern fatwa relaxes this for large towns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) ولا تجوز اقامتها الا للسلطان او لمن امره السلطان. فتح ہو گئے تھے ان میں جمعہ کیوں نہیں ہوا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ شہر میں جمعہ جائز ہے گاؤں میں جائز نہیں ہے۔
كتاب الصلوة
جوانی کے بارے میں منقول ہے کہ وہ ایک قلعہ کا نام ہے اور وہاں شہر تھا۔ قائد امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز ہے جہاں چالیس آدمی نماز پڑھنے والے ہوں ۔ ان کی دلیل ابو داؤد کی یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال ان اول جمعة جمعت في الاسلام بعد جمعة جمعت في مسجد رسول الله له بالمدينة لجمعة جمعت بجواثى قرية من قرى البحرين قال عثمان قرية من قرى عبد القيس (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة في القرى ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جوانی بحرین کے گاؤں کا نام ہے۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ بعض مرتبہ شہر کو بھی قری کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے مکہ مکرمہ کو قرآن نے قریہ کہا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ام عبد الله الدوسية قالت سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول الجمعة واجبة على اهل كل قرية وان لم يكونوا الا ثلاثة ورابعهم امامهم (ب) (دارقطنی ، باب الجمعۃ علی اہل القرية ج ثانی ص سے نمبر ۱۵۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گاؤں میں جمعہ واجب ہے (۲) عن ابی اما مة ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال على الخميس جمعة
ليس فيما دون ذلك (دار قطنی ، ذکر العدد فی الجمعة ج خانی ص ۴ نمبر ۱۵۶۴ را ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة في القرى ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۹) مصر جامع کس کو کہتے ہیں اس کی تعریف اس اثر میں ہے قلت لعطاء ما القرية الجامعة قال ذات الجماعة والامير والقصاص والدور المجتمعة غير المفترقة الآخذ بعضها ببعض كهيئة جده (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ج ثالث ص ۶۸ نمبر ۵۱۷۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بڑی بستی اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں امیر ہو، قصاص اور حدود نافذ کئے جاتے ہوں اور گھر قریب قریب ہوں، خیمہ زنوں کی طرح دور دور گھر نہ ہوں۔ شہر کی دوسری تعریف یہ ہے سمـعـت عـمـر بن دينار يقول اذا كان المسجد يجمع فيه الصلوة فلتصل فيه الجمعة (و) مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القرى الصغارج ثالث ص ۷۰ انمبر ۵۱۸۴) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر تمام آدمی جمع ہو کر
ایک مسجد میں نماز پڑھتے ہوں تو اس میں جمعہ جائز ہے۔
آج کل بڑی بستی میں جمعہ جائز ہونے کا فتوی دیتے ہیں۔
[۳۴۷] (۲) اور نہیں جائز ہے جمعہ قائم کرنا مگر بادشاہ کے لئے یا جس کو بادشاہ نے حکم دیا ہو۔
چونکہ جمعہ میں بہت لوگ ہوتے ہیں، ان کو سنبھالنا سب کا کام نہیں ہے اس لئے بادشاہ یا بادشاہ کا مامور جمعہ قائم کرے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے سال عبد الله بن عمر بن خطاب عن القرى التي بين مكة والمدينة ماترى في الجمعة قال نعم اذا كان حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ سب سے پہلا جمعہ جو اسلام میں پڑھا گیا مدینہ میں مسجد رسول کے جمعہ کے بعد وہ جوائی میں تھا جو بحرین کے گاؤں میں سے ایک گاؤں ہے۔ اور حضرت عثمان نے فرمایا کہ عبد القیس کے گاؤں میں سے ایک گاؤں ہے (ب) حضور گہا کرتے تھے کہ جمعہ واجب ہے ہر گاؤں والوں پر، اگر چہ نہ ہوں مگر تین آدمی اور چوتھا ان کا امام (ج) میں نے عطاء سے پوچھا کہ قریہ جامعہ کیا ہے؟ فرمایا جماعت والے ہوں ، وہاں امیر ہو، قصاص جاری کرتے ہوں، قریب قریب گھر ہوں متفرق نہ ہوں، بعض کے گھر بعض کے ساتھ ملے ہوئے ہوں جدہ شہر کی طرح ( د) عمر بن دینار کہا کرتے تھے ایسی مسجد جس میں جماعت کی نماز ہوتی ہو اس میں جمعہ پڑھ سکتے ہیں۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل)
۲۳۵
كتاب الصلوة
[۳۴۸](۳) ومن شرائطها الوقت فتصح فى وقت الظهر ولا تصح بعده [۳۴۹](۴) ومن
شرائطها الخطبة قبل الصلوة يخطب الامام خطبتين يفصل بينهما بقعدة.
...
عليهم امير فليجمع (الف) ( سن سیتی ، باب العدد الذین از کانوانی قریه وجبت عليهم الجمعة ، ج ثالث ص ۲۵۴، نمبر ۵۶۱۳ ) عن عمر بن العزيز قال لهم حين فرغ من صلوته ان الامام يجمع حيث كان (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الامام مجمع حیث کان ج ثالث ص ۱۶۱ نمبر ۵۱۴۷ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ،۳۹۰ باب الامام يكون مسافر افیم بالموضع ج ثانی ص ۴۷۶، نمبر ۵۴۹۹/ ) بخاری میں یہ جملہ ہے حدثنا ابو خلدة صلى بنا امير الجمعة (بخاری شریف، باب اذا اشتد الحر يوم الجمعۃ ص ۱۲۴ نمبر ۹۰۶ ) ان آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ امیر اور بادشاہ جمعہ قائم کرے۔
وت جہاں امیر اور بادشاہ نہیں ہے وہاں مسلمان جمع ہو کر جس کو امیر چن لے وہ قائم کرائے گا۔
(2) And it is not permissible to establish it except for the sultan or for one whom the sultan has commanded. ... [Complete passage translated as per arabic_clean]
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the condition of the ruler for Jumu'ah. The Hanafi position is that Jumu'ah is only valid if established by the sultan or his deputy. The author explains the reasoning: Jumu'ah involves a large congregation, and managing such a gathering is not everyone's responsibility. He then presents the Shafi'i view that Jumu'ah is valid in any village with forty residents, and their evidence from a hadith about the first Jumu'ah at Jawatha. The Hanafi response distinguishes between village (qarya) and town (mīsr), noting that the term qarya can also refer to a city like Makkah. The definition of qarya jami'a (congregational town) is provided from the effect of 'Ata': it must have a ruler, enforcement of legal penalties, and contiguous houses. The effect of Ibn 'Umar and 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz further support the ruler's role. The concluding fatwa today permits Jumu'ah in large towns even without the ruler's presence, but the original condition is noted.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or his authorized representative who holds authority over the congregational prayer.
قرية جامعة (qarya jami'a): A town where Jumu'ah is valid: must have a ruler, enforcement of penalties, and contiguous houses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is permitted to lead Jumu'ah?
A) The sultan or his appointee
B) Any group of 40 men
C) The eldest man in the village
D) The local imam without permission

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a ruler or his deputy for Jumu'ah; without that, the prayer is not valid as Jumu'ah.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Time Condition for Jumu'ah: Valid Only Within Dhuhr Time
Ruling that Jumu'ah is valid only within Dhuhr time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time condition for Jumu'ah and determine when a Jumu'ah prayer becomes invalid and must be replaced by Dhuhr qada.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is valid only during Dhuhr time; after it expires, one must pray Dhuhr as qada.

This lesson establishes a key condition for Jumu'ah: it must be performed within the time of Dhuhr. We will see the textual proof from the hadith of Anas and an athar from the Companions, and understand the practical implication if the time is missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that among the conditions of Jumu'ah is the time. The ruling is that Jumu'ah is only valid in Dhuhr time.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet ﷺ prayed Jumu'ah when the sun declined (zawal). This indicates the time of Dhuhr.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'حين تميل الشمس' (when the sun declines) establishes that Jumu'ah begins at zawal, the start of Dhuhr time.
This understanding is consistent across all four madhhabs.
4
Note the secondary proof
The athar about Hajjaj delaying Jumu'ah shows that when Dhuhr time expires, the Companions prayed Dhuhr and considered the later Jumu'ah as nafl.
This reinforces that the obligation shifts to Dhuhr qada if time is missed.
5
Apply the ruling
If Jumu'ah is not performed within Dhuhr time, it is not valid. One must instead pray Dhuhr as qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۴۸] (۳) ومن شرائطها الوقت فتصح فى وقت الظهر ولا تصح بعده.
ات ظہر کے وقت میں جمعہ صحیح ہے۔ اس کے بعد صحیح نہیں ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الا الله كان يصلي الجمعة حين تميل الشمس (ج) ( بخاری شریف
، باب وقت الجمعة اذا زالت الشمس ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۱۹۰۴ مسلم شریف ، باب فی وقت صلوۃ الجمعۃ ص ۲۸۳ نمبر ۸۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زوال کے بعد جمعہ کی نماز پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ اور یہ وقت ظہر کا ہے اس لئے ظہر کے وقت میں پڑھا جائے گا۔ ظہر کا وقت نکل جائے تو پھر جمعہ نہیں پڑھے گا بلکہ ظہر کی قضا پڑھے گا۔ اثر میں ہے کان الحجاج يؤخر الجمعة فكنت انا اصلی وابراهیم و سعید بن جبیر فصليا الظهر ثم نتحدث وهو يخطب ثم نصلى معهم ثم نجعلها نافلة (و) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، ۱۳۸۷ الجمعة يؤخرها الامام حتی یذهب وقتها ، ج اول ص ۴۷۴، نمبر ۶ ۵۴۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر کا وقت ختم ہو جائے تو اب جمعہ نہیں پڑھے گا بلکہ ظہر کی نماز قضا پڑھے گا۔
(3) And among its conditions is the time, so it is valid in the time of Dhuhr and not valid after it. ... hadith that he prayed Jumu'ah when the sun declined; this is Dhuhr time. If Dhuhr time expires, then qada' of Dhuhr is prayed.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the time condition for Jumu'ah. The author states that Jumu'ah is only valid within Dhuhr time. He proves this with the hadith of Anas that the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah when the sun declined (zawal), which is the time of Dhuhr. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that if the time of Dhuhr passes, one does not pray Jumu'ah but instead makes up the Dhuhr prayer (qada). The effect of Hajjaj's delay is cited: the companions Ibrahim and Sa'id ibn Jubayr prayed Dhuhr and then joined Hajjaj's Jumu'ah later as a voluntary prayer (nafl). This illustrates that if Jumu'ah time is missed, the obligation shifts to Dhuhr.

Key Terms
الوقت (al-waqt): The time of Dhuhr, from zawal until the length of an object's shadow equals its height.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the time of Dhuhr expires and Jumu'ah has not been prayed, what should a Hanafi do?
A) Pray Jumu'ah anyway as qada
B) Pray Dhuhr as qada
C) Combination of Dhuhr and 'Asr
D) The prayer is dropped

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid within Dhuhr time; if the time expires, one must pray Dhuhr as qada.
